          <div class="t withAv">
           Cunt is considered the worst swear word by many in the UK. Words like bloody, damn, hell, bugger are commonplace and words like
           <a class="forUnlogged" href="#" onclick="users.showLoginForm(window.location);return false;" style="display:inline" title="Register Or Login to View Text">
            ****
           </a>
           ,
           <a class="forUnlogged" href="#" onclick="users.showLoginForm(window.location);return false;" style="display:inline" title="Register Or Login to View Text">
            ****
           </a>
           and bitch are mediocre at best. Calling someone a cunt or a wanker means they've really pissed you off.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Of course if you're an Aussie you use them as greetings for your best mates
          </div>

          <div style="clear:right">
          </div>
          <div class="t withAv">
           For England: There's two approaches to the word cunt, and no grey areas. There are those that are obnoxiously offended by it, to the point where they would recoil in horror.
           <br/>
           Then there's those of us who use it as a friendly descriptive word, and also as an insult. The ticket is in the tone of voice, and what/who it's aimed at. Oi cunt - friend. OI CUNT - person who you do not like. "That cunt just cut me up" - negative sentence subject, negative use "I love you, you cunt" - positive sentence subject, positive use of the word cunt.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           It's like the Inuits and all the different words for snow.
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
